For each place \(\mathfrak{p}\), the character \(\psi_\mathfrak{p}\) induces (via the recipe of §3.1.2) a Haar measure on \(F_\mathfrak{p}\), \(B_\mathfrak{p}\), \(F_\mathfrak{p}^{\times} / F_{\mathfrak{p}}^{\times 2}\), \(\operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathfrak{p}\); we equip \(\mathbb{A}, B_\mathbb{A}\), \(\mathbb{A}^{\times} / \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}\) and \(\operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathbb{A}\) with the corresponding restricted product measures, denoted similarly. This defines the Tamagawa measure on \(\operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathbb{A}\). The quotient measures on \(\mathbb{A}/F\) and \(B_\mathbb{A}/B\) are then probability measures. We likewise equip finite products such as \(F_S\) or \(\operatorname{PB}^\times_S\) with product measures.

We equip \(\mathbb{A}^\times\) with the regularized product of the measures constructed in §3.1.2: for a factorizable function \(f = \prod f_\mathfrak{p} \in C_c^\infty(\mathbb{A}^\times)\) for which \(f_\mathfrak{p} = 1_{\mathcal{O}_\mathfrak{p}^\times}\) for almost all finite primes \(\mathfrak{p}\), we set \[\int_{y \in \mathbb{A}^\times} f(y) \, \frac{d y}{|y|} := \frac{1}{\xi_F^*(1)} \prod_{\mathfrak{p}} \zeta_\mathfrak{p}(1) \int_{y \in F_\mathfrak{p}^\times} f_\mathfrak{p}(y) \, \frac{d y}{|y|}.\] We thereby obtain a quotient Haar \(\frac{d y}{|y|}\) on \(\mathbb{A}^\times / F^\times\) whose pushforward under \(|.| : \mathbb{A}^\times / F^\times \rightarrow \mathbb{R}^\times_+\) is the standard Haar measure \(\frac{d t}{|t|}\) on \(\mathbb{R}^\times_+\), where \(d t\) denotes Lebesgue measure.

The quotient measure on the discrete group \(F^{\times } / F^{\times 2}\) compatible with the squaring map is half the counting measure, i.e., for finitely-supported \(f : F^\times \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\), one has \(\sum_{x \in F^\times } f(x) = \frac{1}{2} \sum_{y \in F^\times / F^{\times 2}} (\sum_{z \in F^\times} f(y z^2) )\). On \(\mathbb{A}^\times / F^\times \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}\), we take the quotient measure \(d_2^\times y\) induced by the exact sequence \(1 \rightarrow F^\times / F^{\times 2} \rightarrow \mathbb{A}^\times / \mathbb{A}^{\times 2} \rightarrow \mathbb{A}^\times / F^\times \mathbb{A}^{\times 2} \rightarrow 1\), where \(F^{\times} / F^{\times 2}\) is equipped with half the counting measure. Thus for \(f \in C_c(\mathbb{A}^\times / \mathbb{A}^{\times 2})\), \[\label{eq:integral-formula-involving-squares}\tag{4.1} \int_{y \in \mathbb{A}^\times / F^\times \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}} \frac{1}{2} \sum_{a \in F^\times / F^{\times 2}} f(a y) \, d_2^\times y = \int_{\mathbb{A}^\times / \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}} f.\] By decomposing the Haar on \(\mathbb{A}^\times\) in two ways, one finds for \(f \in C_c(\mathbb{A}^\times / F^\times)\) that \(\int_{\mathbb{A}^\times / F^\times} f = \int_{x \in \mathbb{A}^\times / F^{\times } \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}} \int_{y \in \mathbb{A}^\times / F^\times} f(x y^2) \, \frac{d y}{|y|} \, d_2^\times s\); moreover, \(\mathop{\mathrm{vol}}(\mathbb{A}^{\times} / F^\times \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}) = 2\). Finally, for \(f \in C_c^\infty([\operatorname{PGL}_2])\), \[\label{eq:sl2-vs-pgl2-integrals}\tag{4.2} \int_{[\operatorname{PGL}_2]} f = \int_{y \in \mathbb{A}^\times / F^\times \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}} \int_{s \in [{\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2]} f(s a(y)) \, d s \, d_2^\times y.\]

§4.1.4. The \(\Xi\)-function

Fix a maximal compact subgroup \(K = \prod K_\mathfrak{p} \leqslant\operatorname{PB}^\times_{\mathbb{A}}\). Let \(\Xi : \operatorname{PB}^\times_{\mathbb{A}} \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) be the product \(\Xi(g) := \prod \Xi_\mathfrak{p}(g_\mathfrak{p})\) of the functions \(\Xi_\mathfrak{p}\) on \(\operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathfrak{p}\) attached in §3.1.5 to the factors \(K_\mathfrak{p}\).

§4.1.5. Conventions

A cusp form is a smooth vector in the Hilbert space \(L^2_{\mathop{\mathrm{cusp}}}([G])\) of square-integrable cuspidal functions. A cuspidal automorphic representation \(\pi\) of \(G_\mathbb{A}\) is the space of smooth vectors in an irreducible subrepresentation of \(L^2_{\mathop{\mathrm{cusp}}}([G])\).

§4.2. Automorphic forms on \(\operatorname{PGL}_2\)

§4.2.1. Fourier expansions

Let \(\varphi : [\operatorname{PGL}_2] \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) be a smooth function. It admits the Fourier expansion \(\varphi(n(x) a(y)) = c_{\varphi}(y) + \sum_{\tau \in F^\times} \psi(\tau x) W_{\varphi}(\tau y)\), where \(c_{\varphi}(y) := \int_{x \in \mathbb{A}/F} \varphi(n(x) a(y)) \,d x\) denotes the constant term and \[W_{\varphi}(y) := \int_{x \in \mathbb{A}/F} \psi(- x) \varphi(n(x) a(y)) \,d x\] denotes the (diagonal restriction of) the Whittaker function. The upper-triangular Borel subgroup of \(\operatorname{PGL}_2(\mathbb{A})\) has dense image in \([\operatorname{PGL}_2]\), so \(\varphi\) is determined by the values \(\varphi(n(x) a(y))\) for \(x \in \mathbb{A}, y \in \mathbb{A}^\times\). Recall that \(\varphi\) is cuspidal if \(c_{\varphi} = 0\); in that case, \(\varphi\) is determined by \(W_\varphi\).

§4.2.2. Kirillov model

Let \(\pi \subseteq L^2([\operatorname{PGL}_2])\) be a cuspidal automorphic representation; it is (the smooth completion of) a restricted tensor product \(\otimes \pi_\mathfrak{p}\), where \(\pi_\mathfrak{p}\) is a generic for every \(\mathfrak{p}\) and unramified for almost all finite \(\mathfrak{p}\). Let \(\mathcal{K}(\pi,\psi) := \{W_\varphi : \varphi \in \pi \}\). The natural map \(\pi \rightarrow \mathcal{K}(\pi,\psi)\) is a linear isomorphism under which the pure tensors in \(\pi\) correspond to the factorizable functions \(W(y) = \prod W_\mathfrak{p}(y_\mathfrak{p})\), where \(W_\mathfrak{p}\) belongs to the local Kirillov model \(\mathcal{K}(\pi_\mathfrak{p},\psi_\mathfrak{p})\) and satisfies \(W_\mathfrak{p} = W_{\pi_\mathfrak{p}}^0\) (see §3.4.3) for almost all finite \(\mathfrak{p}\). The following residue calculation is standard and may be derived from, for instance, (Michel and Venkatesh 2010, Lem 2.2.3).

Lemma 4. Let \(\varphi \in \pi\). The integral \(I(s) := \int_{y \in \mathbb{A}^\times} |W_\varphi(y)|^2 |y|^s \, \frac{d y}{|y|}\) converges absolutely for complex numbers \(s\) with positive real part, extends to a meromorphic function on the complex plane, and satisfies \[\label{eqn:rs-ipf}\tag{4.4} 2 {\mathop{\mathrm{res}}}_{s \rightarrow 0} I(s) = \|\varphi\|^2.\]

§4.2.3. Adjoint \(L\)-function

For \(\pi\), \(S\) as in the lemma of §4.2.2, the partial adjoint \(L\)-function is defined for \(\mathrm{Re}(s) > 1\) by the absolutely-convergent Euler product \(L^{(S)}(\mathop{\mathrm{ad}}\pi,s) := \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} L(\mathop{\mathrm{ad}}\pi_\mathfrak{p},s)\); it continues meromorphically to the complex plane, and is holomorphic for (at least) \(\mathrm{Re}(s) \geqslant 1\) (see (S. Gelbart and Jacquet 1978)).

§4.3. Automorphic forms on \(\operatorname{PB}^\times\)

§4.3.1. Jacquet–Langlands lifts

Let \(\pi = \otimes \pi_\mathfrak{p} \subseteq L^2([\operatorname{PB}^\times])\) be a cuspidal automorphic representation with \(\dim(\pi) > 1\). By (Shimizu 1972, Prop 4), \[\label{eqn:generic-at-each-place-if-not-1-diml}\tag{4.5} \text{$\dim(\pi_\mathfrak{p}) > 1$ for any prime $\mathfrak{p}$ at which $B$ splits.}\] The Jacquet–Langlands lift \(\pi_{\mathop{\mathrm{JL}}} = \otimes \pi_{\mathop{\mathrm{JL}},\mathfrak{p}} \subseteq L^2([\operatorname{PGL}_2])\) is the unique cuspidal automorphic representation for which \(\pi_{\mathop{\mathrm{JL}},\mathfrak{p}} = (\pi_\mathfrak{p})_{\mathop{\mathrm{JL}}}\) for each place \(\mathfrak{p}\). If \(\mathfrak{p}\) is a finite prime at which \(B\) splits and for which \(\pi_\mathfrak{p}\) is unramified, then \((\pi_{\mathop{\mathrm{JL}}})_\mathfrak{p}\) is unramified. The association \(\pi \mapsto \pi_{\mathop{\mathrm{JL}}}\) is injective.

§4.3.2. The pretrace formula

Assume that \(B\) is non-split, so that \([\operatorname{PB}^\times]\) is compact. Fix a maximal compact subgroup \(K\) of \(\operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathbb{A}\). The pretrace formula asserts that for \(f \in C_c^\infty(\operatorname{PB}_\mathbb{A}^\times)\) and \(x \in \operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathbb{A}\), \[\label{eq:pretrace-formula-general}\tag{4.6} \sum_{\pi} \sum_{\varphi} \overline{\varphi (x)} \pi(f) \varphi(x) = \sum_{\gamma \in \operatorname{PB}^\times} f(x^{-1} \gamma x),\] where \(\pi\) traverses the irreducible subrepresentations of \(L^2([\operatorname{PB}^\times])\) and \(\varphi\) traverses an orthonormal basis \(\mathcal{B}(\pi)\) of \(\pi\) consisting of \(K\)-isotypic vectors. Only finitely many summands on the right hand side of \((4.6)\) are nonzero, while the condition on \(\mathcal{B}(\pi)\) implies that the left hand side of \((4.6)\) converges absolutely, or indeed, rapidly: Let \(C(\pi) := \prod_\mathfrak{p} C((\pi_\mathfrak{p})_{\mathop{\mathrm{JL}}}) \in \mathbb{R}_{\geqslant 1}\) denote the analytic conductor of \(\pi\) (see, e.g., (Michel and Venkatesh 2010, sec. 3.1.8, §4.1.4)). By (e.g.) the proof of (Müller 1998, Thm 9.1), one has for each \(A \geqslant 0\) \[\label{eq:rapid-convergence-of-pretrace-formula}\tag{4.7} \sum_{\pi} C(\pi)^A \sum_{\varphi} |\overline{\varphi}(x) \pi(f) \varphi(x)| < \infty.\] Note also that there exists \(A_0 > 3\) so that (see, e.g., (Michel and Venkatesh 2010, (2.15))). \[\label{eq:polynomial-growth-of-reps}\tag{4.8} \sum_{\pi} C(\pi)^{-A_0} < \infty\]

Let \(S\) be a set of places containing the infinite ones. Let \(R \subseteq B\) be a maximal order. For each \(\mathfrak{p} \notin S\), let \(J_\mathfrak{p} \leqslant\operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathfrak{p}\) denote the image of \(R_\mathfrak{p}^\times\), as in §3.4, and set \(J := \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} J_\mathfrak{p}\). Suppose that \(f = f_S \otimes (\otimes_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} T_{y_\mathfrak{p}})\) for some \(f_S \in C_c^\infty(\operatorname{PB}_S^\times)\) and \(y \in \mathbb{A}^\times\), where \(T_{y_\mathfrak{p}}\) is the Hecke kernel as defined in §3.4.1 relative to \(J_\mathfrak{p}\). The formula \((4.6)\) then specializes to \[\sum_\pi (\sum_{\varphi} \overline{\varphi(x)} \pi(f_S) \varphi(x)) \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} \lambda_{\pi_\mathfrak{p}}(T_{y_\mathfrak{p}}) = \sum_{\gamma \in \operatorname{PB}^\times} f_S(x_S^{-1} \gamma x_S) \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} T_{y_\mathfrak{p}}(x_\mathfrak{p}^{-1} \gamma x_\mathfrak{p}),\] where \(\pi \subseteq L^2([\operatorname{PB}^\times])\) now traverses the subrepresentations that are unramified outside \(S\) (i.e., that contain a nonzero \(J\)-fixed vector) and \(\varphi\) traverses an orthonormal basis of \(K\)-isotypic vectors for the \(J\)-fixed subspace \(\pi^J\) of \(\pi\).

§4.3.3. \(L\)-functions

Let \(\pi \subseteq L^2([\operatorname{PB}^\times])\) be a cuspidal automorphic representation with \(\dim(\pi) > 1\). Let \(S\) be a finite set of places containing all infinite places as well as any places at which either \(B\) or \(\pi\) ramifies.

The partial standard \(L\)-function is defined for \(\mathrm{Re}(s) > 1\) by the absolutely-convergent Euler product \(L^{(S)}(\pi,s) := \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} L(\pi_\mathfrak{p},s)\); it continues meromorphically to the complex plane, and is holomorphic for (at least) \(\mathrm{Re}(s) \geqslant 1/2\) (see, e.g., (Bump 1997, vol. 55, sec. 3.5)).

Set \(L^{(S)}(\mathop{\mathrm{ad}}\pi,s) := L^{(S)}(\mathop{\mathrm{ad}}\pi_{\mathop{\mathrm{JL}}}, s)\) (see §4.2.3). By (Hoffstein and Lockhart 1994) (cf. (Blomer and Harcos 2010, sec. 2.9)), one has \[\label{eq:HL}\tag{4.10} C(\pi)^{-\varepsilon} \ll_{\varepsilon} L^{(S)}(\mathop{\mathrm{ad}}\pi,1) \ll_{\varepsilon} C(\pi)^{\varepsilon} \text{ for each } \varepsilon> 0.\]

§4.4. Theta functions

§4.4.1. Metaplectic group

Let \({\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(\mathbb{A})\) denote the metaplectic double cover of \({\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2(\mathbb{A})\); it fits into a short exact sequence \(1 \rightarrow \mu_2 \rightarrow {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(\mathbb{A}) \xrightarrow{\mathop{\mathrm{pr}}} {\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2(\mathbb{A})\). We may identify it with \({\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2(\mathbb{A}) \times \mu_2\), with the group law given by \((s_1,\zeta_1) (s_2,\zeta_2) = (s_1 s_2, \zeta_1 \zeta_2 c(s_1,s_2))\), where \(c\) is the product of the cocycles from §4.4.1. We identify \({\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2(F)\) with its image under the unique splitting \({\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2(F) \hookrightarrow {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(\mathbb{A})\).

We may similarly define \({\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(F_S)\) as a double cover of \({\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2(F_S)\) for any collection \(S\) of places of \(F\).

§4.4.2. Quadratic spaces

We define quadratic spaces \(V\) over \(F\) as in §3.2.1. The relevant examples are still \(V = B, B^0, F\). We equip \(V_\mathbb{A}\) with the \((\psi,b_V)\)-self dual measure \(\mu_V\). That measure is the product of the measures \(\mu_{V_\mathfrak{p}}\) on the local spaces \(V_{\mathfrak{p}}\) attached to \(\psi_\mathfrak{p}\), and is independent of \(\psi\): it assigns volume one to a fundamental domain for \(V_\mathbb{A}/V\).

§4.4.3. Weil representation

For a quadratic space \(V\) over \(F\), the Schwartz–Bruhat space \(\mathcal{S}(V_\mathbb{A})\) factors as the (completed) restricted tensor product \(\mathcal{S}(V_\mathbb{A}) = \otimes \mathcal{S}(V_\mathfrak{p})\). The Weil representation \(\rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}^{\psi,V} : {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(\mathbb{A}) \times \operatorname{O}(V_\mathbb{A}) \rightarrow \mathop{\mathrm{GL}}(\mathcal{S}(V_\mathbb{A}))\) is given by \(\rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}^{\psi,V} = \otimes \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}^{\psi_{\mathfrak{p}},V_{\mathfrak{p}}}\) in the evident sense.

We may similarly define a Weil representation \(\rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}^{\psi,V} : {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(F_S) \times \operatorname{O}(V_S) \rightarrow \mathop{\mathrm{GL}}(\mathcal{S}(V_S))\) for a finite set \(S\) of places of \(F\).

§4.4.4. Theta kernels

Let \(V\) be a quadratic space over \(F\). For \(\phi \in \mathcal{S}(V_\mathbb{A})\), \(s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(\mathbb{A})\) and \(g \in \operatorname{O}(V_\mathbb{A})\), set \(\theta_{\psi}(\phi)(s,g) := \sum_{x \in V} \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}^{\psi,V}(s,g) \phi(x)\). The sum converges absolutely and defines a smooth function \(\theta_{\psi}(\phi) : [{\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2] \times [\operatorname{O}(V)] \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\). We employ notation such as \(\theta_{\psi}(\phi;s,g) := \theta_{\psi}(\phi)(s,g)\). Observe that \[\label{eq:equivariance-theta-kernel}\tag{4.11} \theta_{\psi}(\phi;s s', g g') = \theta_{\psi}(\rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}^{\psi,V}(s',g') \phi;s,g)\]

§4.4.5. Elementary theta functions

Let \(V = F\), regarded as a quadratic subspace of \(B\) as in §3.2.1. In that case, we abbreviate \(\operatorname{O}_1(F) := \operatorname{O}(V) \cong \{\pm 1\}\). For \(\phi \in \mathcal{S}(V_\mathbb{A}) = \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A})\), we denote also by \(\theta_{\psi}(\phi)\) the elementary theta function on \([{\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2]\) obtained by restricting to the first factor of the theta kernel defined in §4.4.4, thus \(\theta_{\psi}(\phi)(s) := \theta_{\psi}(\phi)(s,1) = \sum_{x \in F} \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}^{\psi,F}(s) \phi(x)\). By \((4.11)\), \[\label{eq:equivariance-etf}\tag{4.12} \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{reg}}}(s) \theta_{\psi}(\phi) = \theta_{\psi}(\rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}^{\psi,F}(s) \phi) \text{ for } s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(\mathbb{A}).\] The \(\operatorname{O}_1(F)\)-invariance of the theta kernel says that for \(\phi \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A})\), \[\label{eqn:O1-invariance-elementary-theta-fn}\tag{4.13} \text{$\theta_{\psi}(\phi) = \theta_{\psi}(\phi_-)$ with $\phi_-(x) := \phi(-x)$.}\]

§4.4.6. Ternary theta lifts

Suppose \(V = B^0\). Given \(\Psi : [\operatorname{PB}^\times] \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) and \(\phi \in \mathcal{S}(B^0_\mathbb{A})\) and \(s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(\mathbb{A})\), set \(\theta_{\psi}(\phi,\Psi;s) := \int_{g \in [\operatorname{PB}^\times]} \Psi(g) \theta_{\psi}(\phi;s,\mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g)) \,d g\), where \(\mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}: \operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathbb{A} \xrightarrow{\cong} \mathop{\mathrm{SO}}(B^0_\mathbb{A})\) is the isomorphism induced by the notation of §2. If \(\Psi\) is a cusp form, then the integral converges absolutely and defines a cusp form \(\theta_{\psi}(\phi,\Psi) : [{\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2] \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\). By \((4.11)\), \[\label{eq:equivariance-ttf}\tag{4.14} \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{reg}}}(s) \theta_{\psi}(\phi,\Psi) = \theta_{\psi}(\rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}^{\psi,B^0}(s) \phi, \Psi) \text{ for } s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(\mathbb{A}),\] \[\label{eq:equivariance-ttf-2}\tag{4.15} \theta_{\psi}(\mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g)\phi, \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{reg}}}(g) \Psi) = \theta_{\psi}(\phi, \Psi) \text{ for } g \in \operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathbb{A}.\]

§4.4.7. Factorization

If the quadratic space \(V\) decomposes as the direct sum \(V' \oplus V''\) of quadratic subspaces, then the factorization of the Weil representation (§3.2.4) implies the factorization of theta functions: for \(g = g' \times g'' \in \operatorname{O}(V'_\mathbb{A}) \times \operatorname{O}(V_\mathbb{A} '') \leqslant\operatorname{O}(V_\mathbb{A})\) and \(\phi = \phi ' \otimes \phi '' \in \mathcal{S}(V_\mathbb{A})\) with \(\phi ' \in \mathcal{S}(V'_\mathbb{A}), \phi '' \in \mathcal{S}(V_\mathbb{A} '')\) (see §3.2.4), \[\label{eqn:Factorization-of-theta-fns}\tag{4.16} \theta_{\psi}(\phi;s,g) = \theta_{\psi}(\phi ';s,g') \theta_{\psi}(\phi '';s,g'').\] With \(\phi '_-\) as in \((4.13)\) and notation as in §2, one has \[\label{eq:action-of-S-on-pure-tensors-for-B-0}\tag{4.17} \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) \phi = \phi ' \otimes \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) \phi ''\] \[\label{eq:action-of-S-on-pure-tensors-for-B}\tag{4.18} \mathfrak{S} \phi = \frac{1}{2} ( \phi ' + \phi '_-) \otimes \phi ''.\]

§4.5. Equidistribution of products of pairs of elementary theta functions

The purpose of this section is to recall and apply some results from (Nelson 2021b). Let \(\tau_1,\tau_2 \in F^\times\). Throughout this section, we regard \(\psi,\tau_1,\tau_2,F,B\) as fixed: implied constants may depend upon them without explicit mention. We assume also (for technical convenience) that \(B\) is non-split.

§4.5.1. Some asymptotic notation

Given a topological vector space \(\mathcal{S}\), we adopt the convention (similar to “big O notation”) of denoting by \(\mathcal{C}(\phi)\) any quantity depending continuously upon \(\phi \in \mathcal{S}\); the continuity is assumed uniform in all auxiliary parameters except those explicitly labelled “fixed.” The space \(\mathcal{S}\) itself is always regarded as fixed, of course. This convention applies in particular to Schwartz–Bruhat spaces of finite-dimensional vector spaces over local fields, over finite products of local fields, or over adele rings.

Similarly to the “\(\varepsilon\)-convention” of analytic number theory, we allow the precise meaning of \(\mathcal{C}(\phi)\) to change from one occurrence to the next. When we specifically wish to distinguish between several such quantities, we use the notation \(\mathcal{C} '(\phi), \mathcal{C} ''(\phi)\), and so on.

For example, let \(V\) be a vector space over \(F\) (always assumed finite-dimensional). Let \(\hat{F}\) denote the ring of finite adeles, so that \(\mathbb{A} = F_\infty \times \hat{F}\) with \(F_\infty := \prod_{\mathfrak{p} | \infty} F_\mathfrak{p}\). Similarly, write \(V_\mathbb{A} = V_\infty \times \hat{V}\). The Schwartz–Bruhat space \(\mathcal{S}(V_\mathbb{A})\) factors as the algebraic tensor product \(\mathcal{S}(V_\infty) \otimes \mathcal{S}(\hat{V})\). Suppose given some quantities \(a(\phi;t_1,t_2)\) and \(b(\phi;t_1,t_2)\) depending upon \(\phi \in \mathcal{S}(V_\mathbb{A})\) and some auxiliary parameters \(t_1,t_2\). The notation \[\label{eq:example-a-phi-bounded-by-C-phi}\tag{4.19} a(\phi;t_1,t_2) \ll b(\phi;t_1,t_2) \mathcal{C}(\phi) \text{ for fixed $t_2$ }\] means that for each \(t_2\) and each \(\phi_f \in \mathcal{S}(\hat{V})\), there is a finite collection \(\mathcal{P}\) of polynomials on \(V_\infty\) and a finite collection \(\mathcal{D}\) of translation-invariant differential operators on \(V_\infty\) (thus \(\mathcal{D}\) consists of linear combinations of monomials \(\frac{\partial }{\partial x_{i_1}} \dotsb \frac{\partial }{\partial x_{i_n}}\) with respect to some coordinates \(x_j : V_\infty \rightarrow \mathbb{R}\)) so that for all \(\phi_\infty \in \mathcal{S}(V_\infty)\) and all \(t_1\), \[| a(\phi_\infty \otimes \phi_f;t_1,t_2) | \leqslant|b(\phi_\infty \otimes \phi_f;t_1,t_2)| \sum_{P \in \mathcal{P}} \sum_{D \in \mathcal{D}} \|P D \phi_\infty \|_{L^\infty(V^\infty)}.\] One could just as well write “the functional \(\mathcal{S}(V_\mathbb{A}) \ni \phi \mapsto a(\phi;t_1,t_2)/b(\phi;t_1,t_2)\) is defined and continuous, uniformly in \(t_1\).”

§4.5.2. Simple estimates for lattice sums

Lemma 6. Let \(n \in \mathbb{Z}_{\geqslant 0}\). Let \(A \geqslant 0\) and \(t_0 > 0\) be fixed. For each \(\phi \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^n)\) and \(t > t_0\), one has \(\sum_{v \in \mathbb{Z}^n - \{0\}} |\phi(t v)| \ll |t|^{-A} \mathcal{C}(\phi)\).

Proof. The left hand side of the required estimate is bounded by \[C |t|^{-A} \sup_{x \in \mathbb{R}^n} |x|^{n+1+A} |\phi(x)|\] with \(C := |t_0|^{-(n+1)} \sum_{v \in \mathbb{Z}^n - \{0\}} |v|^{-(n+1+A)} < \infty\). ◻

Lemma 7. Let \(V\) be a vector space over \(F\). Let \(A \geqslant 0\) and \(t_0 > 0\) be fixed. For \(\phi \in \mathcal{S}(V_\mathbb{A})\) and \(y \in \mathbb{A}^\times\) with \(|y| > t_0\), one has \(\sum_{v \in V - \{0\}} |\phi(y v)| \ll |y|^{-A} \mathcal{C}(\phi)\).

Proof. Let \(\mathbb{A}^{(1)} := \{y \in \mathbb{A}^\times : |y| = 1\}\) denote the subgroup of norm one ideles. By the compactness of \(\mathbb{A}^{(1)} / F^\times\) and the continuity of the dilation action of \(\mathbb{A}^\times\) on \(\mathcal{S}(V_\mathbb{A})\), it suffices to consider the case that \(y_\mathfrak{p} = 1\) for all finite \(\mathfrak{p}\) and \(y_\mathfrak{p} = t\) for all infinite \(\mathfrak{p}\), where \(t \in \mathbb{R}_+^\times\) satisfies \(t > t_1 := t_0^{1/[F:\mathbb{Q}]}\). Each \(\phi_f \in \mathcal{S}(\hat{V})\) is bounded and satisfies \(\mathop{\mathrm{supp}}(\phi_f) \cap V \subseteq L\) for some lattice \(L \leqslant V\), so it suffices to show that for fixed \(A \geqslant 0\), fixed \(L \leqslant V\), all \(\phi \in \mathcal{S}(V_\infty)\) and all \(t > t_1\), one has \(\sum_{v \in L - \{0\}} |\phi(t v)| = \operatorname{O}(|t|^{-A} \mathcal{C}(\phi))\). By choosing a \(\mathbb{Z}\)-basis of \(L\), we reduce to Lemma 1. ◻

§4.5.3. Simple estimates for theta functions

Recall that the Iwasawa decomposition asserts that each \(s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2(\mathbb{A})\) may be written in the form \(s = n(x) t(y) k\), where \(x \in \mathbb{A}, y \in \mathbb{A}^\times\) and \(k\) belongs to the standard maximal compact subgroup of \({\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2(\mathbb{A})\). The decomposition is not unique, but the quantities \(x\) and \(|y|\) depend only upon \(s\).

We define \(\mathop{\mathrm{ht}}: [{\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2] \rightarrow \mathbb{R}_{>0}\) by \(\mathop{\mathrm{ht}}(g) := \max_{\gamma \in {\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2(F)} {\mathop{\mathrm{ht}}}_\mathbb{A}(\gamma g)\), where \({\mathop{\mathrm{ht}}}_{\mathbb{A}} : {\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2(\mathbb{A}) \rightarrow \mathbb{R}_{>0}\) is defined with respect to the Iwasawa decomposition \(s = n(x) t(y) k\) by \({\mathop{\mathrm{ht}}}_{\mathbb{A}}(s) := |y|^{1/2}\). One has \(\int_{[{\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2]} {\mathop{\mathrm{ht}}}^{1-\varepsilon} < \infty\) for \(\varepsilon> 0\). Reduction theory says that the image of \(\mathop{\mathrm{ht}}\) is bounded from below by some \(c > 0\) depending only upon \(F\). We extend \(\mathop{\mathrm{ht}}\) via pullback to a map \([{\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2] \rightarrow \mathbb{R}_{>0}\).

Recall that the nontrivial unitary character \(\psi\) of \(\mathbb{A}/F\) is regarded as fixed.

Lemma 8. Let \(A \geqslant 0\) be fixed. Let \(\Psi \in L^1( [\operatorname{PB}^\times])\) with \(\langle \Psi, 1 \rangle = 0\). Let \(\phi \in \mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A}^0)\). For \(s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(\mathbb{A})\), one has \(\theta_{\psi}(\phi,\Psi;s) \ll \mathop{\mathrm{ht}}(s)^{-A} \mathcal{C}(\phi) \|\Psi \|_{L^1}\).

Proof. Since \(\Psi\) has mean zero, \[\theta_{\psi}(\phi,\Psi;s) = \int_{g \in [\operatorname{PB}^\times]} \Psi(g) \sum_{v \in V - \{0\}} \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}^{\psi,V}(s,\mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g)) \phi(v) \,d g.\] By the Iwasawa decomposition and reduction theory, we may assume that \(s = n(x) t(y) k\) with \(|y| \gg 1\). Since \(B\) is non-split, we may fix a compact subset \(U\) of \(\operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathbb{A}\) containing a fundamental domain for \([\operatorname{PB}^\times]\). Then \[|\theta_{\psi}(\phi,\Psi;s)| \leqslant\|\Psi \|_{L^1} |y|^{3/2} \sup_{g \in U} \sum_{v \in B^0 - \{0\}} |\rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}^{\psi,B^0}(k,\mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g)) \phi(y v)|.\] Since the Weil representation is continuous (Weil 1964, sec. 39), we may reduce to the case \(k = 1\) and \(g = 1\), in which the required estimate follows from Lemma 2 of §4.5.2. ◻

Lemma 9. For \(\phi \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A})\) and \(s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(\mathbb{A})\), one has \(\theta_{\psi}(\phi;s) \ll \mathop{\mathrm{ht}}(s)^{1/4} \mathcal{C}(\phi)\).

Proof. We argue as in the proof of Lemma 1, but take into account the contribution from \(0 \in F\) to the definition of \(\theta_{\psi}(\phi)\). ◻

§4.5.4. Main estimate: the case of pure tensors

Lemma 5. Let \(\phi_1', \phi_2' \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A})\) and \(\phi_1'', \phi_2'' \in \mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A}^0)\). Let \(\Psi_1, \Psi_2 : [\operatorname{PB}^\times] \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) be integrable functions of mean zero. Let \(\tau_1, \tau_2 \in F^\times\) be fixed. Abbreviate \(\theta_i := \theta_{\psi^{\tau_i}}(\phi_i')\) and \(h_i := \theta_{\psi^{\tau_i}}(\phi_i'',\Psi_i)\). Then for all \(s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(\mathbb{A})\), \[\langle \theta_1 \cdot \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{reg}}}(s) h_1, \theta_2 \cdot \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{reg}}}(s) h_2 \rangle = \langle \theta_1, \theta_2 \rangle \langle h_1, h_2 \rangle + \operatorname{O}\left(\Xi(s) \prod_{i=1,2} \mathcal{C}(\phi_i') \mathcal{C}(\phi_i'') \|\Psi_i\|_{L^1} \right).\]

Proof. The main result of (Nelson 2021b) gives an estimate essentially of the required shape, but instead with the error term \(\Xi(s) \mathcal{S}(\phi_1') \mathcal{S}(\phi_2') \mathcal{S}^{\mathbf{X}}(h_1 \overline{h_2})\), where \(\mathcal{S}, \mathcal{S}^{\mathbf{X}}\) are the adelic Sobolev norms defined in loc. cit. and (Michel and Venkatesh 2010, sec. 2). By the cuspidality of \(h_1, h_2\) and axioms (S3b) and (S4e) of (Michel and Venkatesh 2010), we may replace the expression \(\mathcal{S}^{\mathbf{X}}(h_1 \overline{h_2})\) first with \(\mathcal{S}^{\mathbf{X}}(h_1) \mathcal{S}^{\mathbf{X}}(h_2)\) and then with \(\mathcal{S}(h_1) \mathcal{S}(h_2)\). Our task thereby reduces to showing for \(i=1,2\) that \(\mathcal{S}(\phi_i') \ll \mathcal{C}(\phi_i')\) and \(\mathcal{S}(h_i) \ll \mathcal{C}(\phi_i'') \|\Psi_i\|_{L^1}\). The first of these estimates, i.e., that the norms \(\mathcal{S}\) are continuous, follows readily from the definitions of those norms. The second estimate follows similarly, using Lemma 1 of §4.5.3. ◻

§4.5.5. Factorization

Let \(V', V''\) be vector spaces over \(F\) and \(V := V' \oplus V''\).

Lemma 6. Let \(\ell : \mathcal{S}(V_\mathbb{A} ') \otimes \mathcal{S}(V_\mathbb{A} '') \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) be an algebraic linear functional on the algebraic tensor product of Schwartz–Bruhat spaces satisfying an estimate of the form \[\ell(\phi' \otimes \phi '') \ll \mathcal{C}'(\phi ') \mathcal{C}''(\phi '')\] on pure tensors. Then \(\ell\) extends to a continuous functional \(\ell : \mathcal{S}(V_\mathbb{A}) \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) satisfying \[\ell(\phi) \ll \mathcal{C}(\phi)\] for all \(\phi \in \mathcal{S}(V_\mathbb{A})\), where \(\mathcal{C}\) depends only upon \(\mathcal{C} '\) and \(\mathcal{C} ''\).

Proof. This is essentially the Schwartz kernel theorem, as extended by Bruhat (Bruhat 1961, sec. 5), and follows from a standard “square-root of a partition of unity” argument. ◻

§4.5.6. Main estimate: the general case

Temporarily denote by \(\mathcal{A}_0\) the space of integrable functions \(\Psi : [\operatorname{PB}^\times] \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) of mean zero. Let \(\mathcal{E}_{\tau_1,\tau_2} : \mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A}) \otimes \mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A}) \otimes \mathcal{A}_0 \otimes \mathcal{A}_0 \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) denote the sesquilinear form given for \(\phi_i = \phi_i' \otimes \phi_i'' \in \mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A})\) with \(\phi_1',\phi_2' \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}), \phi_1'',\phi_2'' \in \mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A}^0)\) by \[\begin{align} \mathcal{E}_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\phi_1, \phi_2, \Psi_1, \Psi_2) := \langle \theta_1 h_1, \theta_2 h_2 \rangle - \langle \theta_1, \theta_2 \rangle \langle h_1, h_2 \rangle, \end{align}\] where we abbreviate \(\theta_i := \theta_{\tau_i}(\phi_i')\) and \(h_i := \theta_{\tau_i}(\phi_i'',\Psi_i)\). (The definition makes sense: a priori estimates as in §4.5.3 and the density of \(\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}) \otimes \mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A}^0)\) in \(\mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A})\) allow us to extend \(\mathcal{E}_{\tau_1,\tau_2}\) continuously from its initial domain.)

Proposition 1. For \(\phi_1, \phi_2 \in \mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A}), \Psi_1,\Psi_2 \in \mathcal{A}_0\) and \(s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(\mathbb{A})\), one has with \(\rho_0^{\tau}(s) := \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}^{\psi^{\tau}, B^0}(s)\) the estimate \[\mathcal{E}_{\tau_1,\tau_2}((1 \otimes \rho_0^{\tau_1}(s))\phi_1, (1 \otimes \rho_0^{\tau_2}(s))\phi_2, \Psi_1,\Psi_2) \ll \Xi(s) \prod_{j=1,2} \mathcal{C}(\phi_j) \|\Psi_j\|_{L^1}.\] The implied constant and the uniformity of the continuity of \(\mathcal{C}(\phi_j)\) depend at most upon \(\psi,\tau_1,\tau_2,F,B\). The operator \(1 \otimes \rho_0^{\tau_1}(s)\) is defined as in §3.2.4.

Proof. The lemma of §4.5.5 reduces the general case of Proposition 1 to the special case in which \(\phi_i = \phi_i' \otimes \phi_i''\) for \(i=1,2\), which follows from the lemma of §4.5.4 upon recalling from \((4.14)\) that \(\theta_{\psi_\tau}\) intertwines \(\rho_{0}^{\tau}\) with \(\rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{reg}}}\). ◻

§4.5.7. Invariance properties

We record these for later use.

Lemma 7. For \(g_1, g_2 \in \operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathbb{A}\) and \(s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(\mathbb{A})\), one has \[\begin{align} \mathcal{E}_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\phi_1, \phi_2, \Psi_1, \Psi_2) &= \mathcal{E}_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\mathfrak{S} \phi_1, \phi_2, \Psi_1, \Psi_2) \\ &= \mathcal{E}_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\phi_1, \mathfrak{S} \phi_2, \Psi_1, \Psi_2) \\ &= \mathcal{E}_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g_1) \phi_1, \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g_2) \phi_2, \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{reg}}}(g_1) \Psi_1, \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{reg}}}(g_2)\Psi_2) \\ &= \mathcal{E}_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}^{\psi^{\tau_1},B}(s) \phi_1, \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}^{\psi^{\tau_2},B}(s) \phi_2, \Psi_1, \Psi_2). \end{align}\]

Proof. The first two identities follow from \((4.18)\) and \((4.13)\), the remaining from \((4.12)\), \((4.14)\), \((4.15)\), \((4.17)\), \((4.18)\) and the translation invariance of the Petersson inner product. ◻

§4.6. Simillitude theta functions

§4.6.1. Weil representation

For each place \(\mathfrak{p}\) of \(F\), let \(\Omega_{\mathfrak{p}}\) denote the representation of \(\operatorname{PGL}_2(F_{\mathfrak{p}}) \times \mathop{\mathrm{PGO}}(B_\mathfrak{p})\) attached as in §3.2.5 to the tuple \((F_\mathfrak{p},B_{\mathfrak{p}},\psi_{\mathfrak{p}})\). Let \(\Omega\) denote the restricted tensor product of the spaces \(\Omega_{\mathfrak{p}}\) with respect to the distinguished elements, which we denote now by \(\phi_{\mathfrak{p}}^0 \in \Omega_{\mathfrak{p}}\). We may and shall identify \(\Omega\) with the space of functions \(\phi : \mathbb{A}^\times \times B_\mathbb{A} \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) such that

  • For each \(t \in \mathbb{A}^\times\), the function \(\phi[t] : B_\mathbb{A} \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) given by \(\phi[t](x) := \phi(t,x)\) belongs to the Schwartz–Bruhat space \(\mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A})\);

  • \(\phi(z^2 t, x) = \phi(t, z x)\) for all \(z,t \in \mathbb{A}^\times, x \in B_\mathbb{A}\).

  • There is a compact subset \(C\) of \(\mathbb{A}^\times / \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}\) such that \(\phi[t] = 0\) for all \(t \notin C\) (i.e., for all \(t \in \mathbb{A}^\times\) whose image in \(\mathbb{A}^\times / \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}\) lies outside \(C\));

  • There is an open subgroup \(U\) of \(\mathbb{A}^\times / \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}\) such that \(\phi[t u] = \phi[t]\) for all \(t \in \mathbb{A}^\times, u \in U\).

We equip \(\Omega\) with the invariant hermitian norm \(\|.\|\) obtained by tensoring those on the factors \(\Omega_\mathfrak{p}\), thus \[\label{eqn:inner-product-on-Omega-1-adelic}\tag{4.22} \|\phi\|^2_{\Omega} := \int_{t \in \mathbb{A}^\times / \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}} |t|^2 \int_{x \in B_\mathbb{A}} |\phi|^2(t,x) \, d x \, d_2^\times t.\] The group \(\operatorname{PGL}_2(\mathbb{A}) \times \mathop{\mathrm{PGO}}(B_\mathbb{A})\) acts on \(\Omega\) by the representation \(\rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}\) obtained as the restricted tensor product of those defined in §3.2.5. We define \(\mathfrak{S} : \Omega \rightarrow \Omega\) and (for \(g \in \operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathbb{A}\)) \(\mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) : \Omega \rightarrow \Omega\) as in §3.2.5. Note that \(\mathfrak{S}\) does not preserve pure tensors: for \(\phi = \otimes \phi_\mathfrak{p} \in \Omega\), \[\begin{align} \mathfrak{S} \phi (t,x) &= (\phi (t,x) + \phi (t,x - \mathop{\mathrm{tr}}(x)))/2, \\ \otimes \mathfrak{S} \phi_\mathfrak{p}(x,t) &= \prod (\phi (t_\mathfrak{p},x_\mathfrak{p}) + \phi (t_\mathfrak{p},x_\mathfrak{p} - \mathop{\mathrm{tr}}(x_\mathfrak{p} )))/2, \end{align}\] and in general, these are not the same. They do coincide if \(\# \{ \mathfrak{p} : \mathfrak{S} \phi_\mathfrak{p} \neq \phi_\mathfrak{p} \} \leqslant 1\).

§4.6.2. Theta functions

For \(\phi \in \Omega\), \(s \in \operatorname{PGL}_2(\mathbb{A}), g \in \mathop{\mathrm{PGO}}(B_\mathbb{A})\), set \[\label{defn:theta-knerle-for-Omega}\tag{4.23} \Theta(\phi;s,g) := \frac{1}{2} \sum_{\tau \in F^\times / F^{\times 2}} \sum_{x \in B} \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}(s,g) \phi(\tau,x).\] The sum is well-defined, converges absolutely and defines a smooth function \(\Theta(\phi)\) on \([\operatorname{PGL}_2] \times [\mathop{\mathrm{PGO}}(B)]\). For a cusp form \(\Psi : [\operatorname{PB}^\times] \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) and \(s \in \operatorname{PGL}_2(\mathbb{A})\), set \[\Theta(\phi,\Psi;s) := \int_{g \in [\operatorname{PB}^\times]} \Psi(g) \Theta(\phi;s,\mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g)) \, d g.\] The integral (together with similar integrals below) converges absolutely and defines a cusp form \(\Theta(\phi,\Psi) : [\operatorname{PGL}_2] \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\).

Remark 3. \(\Theta(\phi,\Psi)\) is not a theta lift in the traditional sense: the integral in its definition is with respect to the orthogonal group of \(B^0\) rather than that of \(B\).

§4.6.3. Fourier expansion

Let \(\phi \in \Omega\), and let \(\Psi : [\operatorname{PB}^\times] \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) be a cusp form.

Lemma 8. For \(x \in \mathbb{A}\), \(y \in \mathbb{A}^\times\), one has \[\Theta(\phi,\Psi;n(x) a(y)) = \sum_{\tau \in F^\times} \psi(\tau x) W(\Theta(\phi,\Psi), \tau y)\] where \(W(\Theta(\phi,\Psi),y) := \int_{g \in [\operatorname{PB}^\times]} \Psi(g) \sum_{\gamma \in \operatorname{PB}^\times} |y| \phi(y \mathop{\mathrm{nr}}(\gamma)^{-1}, g^{-1} \gamma g) \,d g\).

Proof. By direct unfolding as in (Shimizu 1972), one has for \(g \in \operatorname{PB}^\times_{\mathbb{A}}\) that \[\begin{split} \Theta(\phi, n(x) a(y);\mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g)) &= \frac{1}{2} \sum_{\tau \in F^\times / F^{\times 2}} |y| \phi(\tau y,0) \\ &\quad + \sum_{\tau \in F^\times} \psi(\tau x) W(\Theta(\phi),\mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g),\tau y), \end{split}\] where \(W(\Theta(\phi),\mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g),y) := \sum_{\gamma \in \operatorname{PB}^\times} |y| \phi(y \mathop{\mathrm{nr}}(\gamma)^{-1}, g^{-1} \gamma g)\). We conclude by integrating against \(\Psi\). ◻

§4.6.4. Restriction to \({\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2\)

Let \(\phi, \Psi\) be as above.

Lemma 9. Let \(y \in \mathbb{A}^\times\). Suppose that \(\phi [y] = \phi '[y] \otimes \phi ''[y]\) for some \(\phi '[y] \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A})\), \(\phi ''[y] \in \mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A}^0)\). Then for \(s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2(\mathbb{A})\), \[\label{eqn:simliitude-theta-expand-as-sum-of-pure-tensors-and-over-a}\tag{4.25} \Theta(\phi,\Psi;s a(y)) = \frac{1}{2} \sum_{\tau \in F^\times \backslash F^{\times 2}} |y| \theta_{\psi^\tau}(\phi'[\tau y];s) \theta_{\psi^\tau}(\phi''[\tau y],\Psi;s).\]

Proof. We derive first using \((4.23)\) that for \(g \in \operatorname{O}(B_{\mathbb{A}})\), \[\Theta(\phi;s a(y),g) = \frac{1}{2} \sum_{\tau \in F^\times \backslash F^{\times 2}} |y| \theta_{\psi^\tau}(\phi[\tau y];s,g),\] hence by \((4.16)\) that for \(g \in \operatorname{O}(B_\mathbb{A}^0)\), \[\Theta(\phi;s a(y),g) = \frac{1}{2} \sum_{\tau \in F^\times \backslash F^{\times 2}} |y| \theta_{\psi^\tau}(\phi'[\tau y];s) \theta_{\psi^\tau}(\phi''[\tau y];s,g).\] We integrate against \(\Psi\) to conclude. ◻

§4.6.5. Unfolding the inner product

Let \(\phi_1, \phi_2 \in \Omega\). Let \(\Psi_1, \Psi_2 : [\operatorname{PB}^\times] \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) be cusp forms.

Lemma 10. Suppose that for each \(y \in \mathbb{A}^\times\), one has \(\phi_i [y] = \phi_i '[y] \otimes \phi_i ''[y]\) for some \(\phi_i '[y] \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A})\), \(\phi_i ''[y] \in \mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A}^0)\). Then the following identity holds, with both sides converging absolutely: \[\label{eq:inner-product-pgl2-made-into-sl2}\tag{4.26} \begin{split} &\langle \Theta(\phi_1,\Psi_1), \Theta(\phi_2,\Psi_2) \rangle_{\operatorname{PGL}_2} \\ &\quad = \int_{y \in \mathbb{A}^\times / F^\times \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}} |y|^2 \frac{1}{2^2} \sum_{\tau_1,\tau_2 \in F^\times / F^{\times 2}} \langle \theta_1 h_1, \theta_2 h_2 \rangle_{{\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2} \, d_2^\times y, \end{split}\] \[\label{eq:thet-:=-thet}\tag{4.27} \theta_i := \theta_{\psi^{\tau_i}}(\phi_i'[\tau_i y]), \quad h_i := \theta_{\psi^{\tau_i}}(\phi_i''[\tau_i y],\Psi_i).\]

Proof. The left hand side is an inner product of cusp forms, hence convergent. On the right hand side, we may replace the \(y\)-integral by a finite sum, since the domain \(\mathbb{A}^{\times} / F^{\times } \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}\) is compact and the integrand is invariant under an open subgroup. For individual \(y\), the sum over \(\tau_1, \tau_2\) has only finitely many nonzero summands, each of which consists of an inner product whose convergence is clear (see §4.5.3). The expansion \((4.25)\) implies for \(y \in \mathbb{A}^\times, s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2(\mathbb{A})\) that \(\Theta(\phi_i,\Psi_i,a(y) s) = \frac{1}{2} \sum _{\tau_i \in F^\times / F^{\times 2} } |y| \theta_i(s) h_i(s)\), so the required identity follows from the formula \((4.2)\) relating integrals over \([\operatorname{PGL}_2]\) and \([{\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2]\). ◻

Remark 4. In this paper, we consider several expressions shaped like the right hand side of \((4.26)\). On a first (or perhaps on any) reading, one should focus on the contributions from \(y = \tau_1 = \tau_2 = 1\); under some class number and unit group restrictions, these turns out to be the relevant ones for our applications. (We considered imposing such restrictions for the sake of presentation, but found that doing so obfuscated rather than simplified.)

§4.7. Inner product formulas

§4.7.1. Elementary theta functions

We recall part of (Nelson 2021b, Thm 2).

Lemma 11. Suppose \(\phi_1, \phi_2 \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A})\) satisfy \(\phi_1(x) = \phi_1(-x), \phi_2(x) = \phi_2(-x)\). Let \(\tau_1, \tau_2 \in F^\times\). Set \(\theta_1 := \theta_{\psi^{\tau_1}}(\phi_1), \theta_2 := \theta_{\psi^{\tau_1}}(\phi_2)\). Then \(\langle \theta_1, \theta_2 \rangle_{{\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2}= 0\) unless \(\tau_1 = \tau_2\), in which case \(\langle \theta_1, \theta_2 \rangle_{{\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2} = 2 \langle \phi_1, \phi_2 \rangle_{L^2(\mathbb{A})}\).

§4.7.2. Ternary theta lifts

As in (Nelson 2016, sec. 12.3), we explicate Gan–Takeda (Gan and Takeda 2011, Thm 6.6) (compare with (Qiu 2014, Prop 2.8 (i))).

Lemma 12. Let \(\pi_1, \pi_2 \subseteq L^2([\operatorname{PB}^\times])\) be cuspidal automorphic representations that are not one-dimensional. Let \(\Psi_1 \in \pi_1, \Psi_2 \in \pi_2\) and \(\phi_1, \phi_2 \in \mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A}^0)\). Let \(\tau \in F^\times\). Set \(h_i := \theta_{\psi^{\tau}}(\phi_i,\Psi_i)\) for \(i=1,2\).

  1. If \(\pi_1 \neq \pi_2\), then \(\langle h_1, h_2 \rangle_{{\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2} = 0\).

  2. Suppose \(\pi_1 = \pi_2 =: \pi\). Let \(S\) be a finite set of places of \(F\) that contains all archimedean places, as well as any finite places at which \(B\) ramifies, and that is sufficiently large in terms of \(\Psi_i, \phi_i\). Then \(\langle h_1, h_2 \rangle_{{\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2}\) equals \[\frac{L^{(S)}(\pi,\tfrac{1}{2})}{\zeta_F^{(S)}(2)} \left(\prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} \mathop{\mathrm{vol}}(K_\mathfrak{p}) \right) \int_{g \in \operatorname{PB}^\times_S} \langle \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) \phi_1, \phi_2 \rangle_{L^2(B_\mathbb{A}^0)} \langle \pi(g) \Psi_1, \Psi_2 \rangle_{\operatorname{PB}^\times} \, d g\] with \(L^{(S)}(\pi,\tfrac{1}{2})\) as in §4.3.3.

§4.7.3. Induction to \(\Omega\)

We now combine the previous two lemmas and sum them up. Temporarily denote by \(\mathcal{A}_0\) the space of cusp forms \(\Psi : [\operatorname{PB}^\times] \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) that are orthogonal to all one-dimensional representations. For \(\tau_1, \tau_2 \in F^\times\), let \(\mathfrak{m} : \Omega \otimes \Omega \otimes \mathcal{A}_0 \otimes \mathcal{A}_0 \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) denote the sesquilinear form given for \(\phi_1, \phi_2 \in \Omega\) admitting factorizations \(\phi_i[y] = \phi_i'[y] \otimes \phi_i''[y]\) by \[\mathfrak{m}(\phi_1,\phi_2,\Psi_1,\Psi_2) := \int_{y \in \mathbb{A}^\times / F^{\times } \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}} |y|^2 \frac{1}{2^2} \sum_{\tau_1,\tau_2 \in F^\times / F^{\times 2}} \langle \theta_1, \theta_2 \rangle \langle h_1, h_2 \rangle \, d_2^\times y,\] with \(\theta_i, h_j\) as in \((4.27)\). The relevance of \(\mathfrak{m}\) may be inferred from §4.6.5.

The definition makes sense: as in the proof of §4.6.5, the \(y\)-integral is really a finite sum, and the sum over \(\tau_1, \tau_2\) has only finitely many nonzero summands. Each summand defines a sesquilinear form on \(\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A}) \otimes \mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A}^0) \otimes \mathcal{A}_0\) that extends continuously to \(\mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A}) \otimes \mathcal{A}_0\) by the a priori estimates of §4.5.3.

Lemma 13. Let \(\pi_1, \pi_2 \subseteq L^2([\operatorname{PB}^\times])\) be cuspidal automorphic representations that are not one-dimensional. Let \(\Psi_1 \in \pi_1, \Psi_2 \in \pi_2\). Let \(\phi_1, \phi_2 \in \Omega\).

  1. If \(\pi_1 \neq \pi_2\) then \(\mathfrak{m}(\phi_1,\phi_2,\Psi_1,\Psi_2) = 0\).

  2. Suppose \(\pi_1 = \pi_2 =: \pi\). Let \(S\) be a large enough finite set of places. Then \(\mathfrak{m}(\phi_1,\phi_2,\Psi_1,\Psi_2)\) equals \[\frac{L^{(S)}(\pi,\tfrac{1}{2})}{\zeta_F^{(S)}(2)} \left(\prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} \mathop{\mathrm{vol}}(K_\mathfrak{p}) \right) \int_{g \in \operatorname{PB}^\times_S} \langle \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) \mathfrak{S} \phi_1, \mathfrak{S} \phi_2 \rangle_{\Omega} \langle \pi(g) \Psi_1, \Psi_2 \rangle_{\operatorname{PB}^\times} \,d g.\]

Proof. It suffices to consider the case that \(\phi_1, \phi_2\) admit factorizations as in the definition of \(\mathfrak{m}\). By \((4.13)\) and \((4.18)\), we may assume that \(\mathfrak{S} \phi_i = \phi_i\), or equivalently, that \(\phi_i'(t,x) = \phi_i'(t,-x)\). By the lemmas of §4.7.1 and §4.7.2, we have \(\langle \theta_1, \theta_2 \rangle = 0\) unless \(\tau_1 = \tau_2\) and then \(\langle h_1, h_2 \rangle = 0\) unless \(\pi_1 = \pi_2\); in that case, the formulas from those lemmas and the identities \[\langle \phi_1'[y \tau], \phi_2'[y \tau] \rangle_{L^2(\mathbb{A})} \langle \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) \phi_1''[y \tau], \phi_2''[y \tau] \rangle_{L^2(B_\mathbb{A}^0)}\] \[= \langle \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) \phi_1[y \tau], \phi_2[y \tau] \rangle_{L^2(B_\mathbb{A})}\] and (see \((4.1)\), \((4.22)\)) \[\int_{y \in \mathbb{A}^{\times} / F^\times \mathbb{A}^{\times 2} } |y|^2 \frac{1}{2} \sum_{\tau \in F^\times / F^{\times 2}} \langle \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) \phi_1[y \tau], \phi_2[y \tau] \rangle_{L^2(B_\mathbb{A})} \, d_2^\times y\] \[= \int_{y \in \mathbb{A}^{\times} / \mathbb{A}^{\times 2} } |y|^2 \langle \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) \phi_1[y], \phi_2[y] \rangle_{L^2(B_\mathbb{A})} \, d_2^\times y = \langle \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) \phi_1, \phi_2 \rangle_{\Omega}\] combine to give the required conclusion. ◻

§5. Estimates for general quantum variance sums

In this section, we introduce general families of quantum variance sums, propose a candidate for their leading asymptotics, and state a general “estimate” comparing the two.

§5.1. Notation

Let \(F\) be a number field with adele ring \(\mathbb{A}\). Fix a nontrivial unitary character \(\psi\) of \(\mathbb{A}/F\). Let \(B\) be a non-split quaternion algebra over \(F\). Fix a maximal order \(R \subseteq B\) and a finite set \(S\) of places of \(F\), containing all archimedean places as well as any finite places at which \(B\) ramifies. Retain the (unsurprising) notation of §4.1.

Since \(B\) is non-split, the quotient \([\operatorname{PB}^\times]= \operatorname{PB}^\times \backslash \operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathbb{A}\) is compact, and so \(L^2([\operatorname{PB}^\times])\) is completely reducible. Let \(A^{\flat}\) denote the set of irreducible subrepresentations of the Hilbert space \(L^2([\operatorname{PB}^\times])\). For each \(\pi^{\flat} \in A^{\flat}\), let \(\pi \leqslant\pi^{\flat}\) denote the subspace of smooth vectors. Set \(A := \{\pi : \pi^\flat \in A^{\flat}\}\). Let \(\mathcal{A}\) denote the algebraic direct sum \(\oplus_{\pi \in A} \pi\), regarded as a pre-unitary representation of the group \(\operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathbb{A}\).

We introduce the following additional notation:

  • \(K = \prod K_\mathfrak{p}\): a maximal compact subgroup of \(\operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathbb{A}\). For \(\mathfrak{p} \notin S\), we assume that \(K_\mathfrak{p} \leqslant\operatorname{PB}^\times_{\mathfrak{p}}\) is the image of \(R_\mathfrak{p}^\times\).

  • \(\mathcal{A}_0 \leqslant\mathcal{A}\): the orthogonal complement of the one-dimensional subrepresentations. (We had earlier, in §4.5 and §4.7.3, used the same symbol to denote some larger spaces than what we call here \(\mathcal{A}_0\). This abuse of notation should introduce no confusion.)

  • \(A_0 := \{\pi \in A : \pi \subseteq \mathcal{A}_0\} = \{\pi \in A : \dim(\pi) > 1\}\), so that \(\mathcal{A}_0 = \oplus_{\pi \in A_0} \pi\).

  • \(\mathcal{A}^S := \{\varphi \in \mathcal{A} : \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{reg}}}(k) \varphi = \varphi \text{ for all } k \in K_\mathfrak{p}, \mathfrak{p} \notin S \}, \mathcal{A}_0^S := \mathcal{A}_0 \cap \mathcal{A}^S\): the “unramified outside \(S\)” subspaces of \(\mathcal{A}, \mathcal{A}_0\).

  • \(A^S := \{\pi \in A : \pi \cap \mathcal{A}^S \neq \{0\}\}, {A}_0^S := {A}^S \cap {A}_0\): the subsets consisting of those \(\pi\) that are unramified outside \(S\).

  • \(\mathcal{B}(V)\), for \(V\) a \(K\)-invariant subspace of \(\mathcal{A}\): an orthonormal basis for the closure of \(V\) that consists of \(K\)-isotypic elements of \(V\).

Fix Haar measures on \(\operatorname{PB}^\times_S\) and \([\operatorname{PB}^\times]\); we do not require any compatibility between them. Because \(B\) is non-split, each \(\pi \in A_0\) is cuspidal. Let \(L^{(S)}(\pi,s)\), \(L^{(S)}(\mathop{\mathrm{ad}}\pi,s)\) be as in §4.3.3.

§5.2. Key definitions

By \((4.7)\), \((4.8)\) and \((4.10)\), the sums considered in the definitions to follow converge absolutely.

§5.2.1. The basic distributions

For \(\pi \in A^S\), define \(\omega_\pi : C_c^\infty(\operatorname{PB}^\times_S) \otimes \mathcal{A}^S \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) by \(\omega_\pi(f,\Psi) := \sum_{\varphi \in \mathcal{B}(\pi \cap \mathcal{A}^S)} \langle \varphi, \Psi \cdot \pi(f) \varphi \rangle\). The definition is independent of the choice of orthonormal basis.

Example 1. If \(\pi(f) = 0\), then \(\omega_\pi(f,\Psi) = 0\). If \(\pi(f)\) is the orthogonal projector onto a one-dimensional subspace \(\mathbb{C} \varphi\) of \(\pi\) with unit basis vector \(\varphi\), then \(\omega_\pi(f,\Psi) = \langle \varphi, \Psi \varphi \rangle\).

§5.2.2. Quantum variance sums

For \(f \in C_c^\infty(\operatorname{PB}^\times_S)\), define the sesquilinear form \(\mathcal{V}_f : \mathcal{A}_0^S \otimes \mathcal{A}_0^S \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) by \[\mathcal{V}_f(\Psi_1,\Psi_2) := \sum_{\pi \in A_0^S} L^{(S)}(\mathop{\mathrm{ad}}\pi,1) \omega_\pi( f,\Psi_1) \overline{ \omega_\pi( f,\Psi_2) }.\]

§5.2.3. Proposed limiting variance

For \(f \in C_c^\infty(\operatorname{PB}^\times_S)\), define the sesquilinear form \(\mathcal{M}_f : \mathcal{A}_0^S \otimes \mathcal{A}_0^S \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) by requiring for \(\Psi_1 \in \pi_1 \in A_0^S, \Psi_2 \in \pi_2 \in A_0^S\) that \(\mathcal{M}_f(\Psi_1,\Psi_2) := 0\) unless \(\pi_1 = \pi_2 =: \pi\), in which case \[\mathcal{M}_f(\Psi_1,\Psi_2) := c_3 L^{(S)}(\pi,\tfrac{1}{2}) \int_{g \in \operatorname{PB}^\times_S} \langle \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) \mathfrak{S} f, \mathfrak{S} f \rangle_{L^2(\operatorname{PB}^\times_S)} \langle \pi(g) \Psi_1, \Psi_2 \rangle_{\operatorname{PB}^\times} \, d g\] where \[\label{eq:defn-of-c}\tag{5.1} c_3 := \zeta_F^{(S)}(2) \mathop{\mathrm{vol}}([\operatorname{PB}^\times])^{-1}.\] The integral converges absolutely (see §3.1.6, §3.4.4).

§5.2.4. Thickening \(\operatorname{PB}^\times\) inside \(B\)

Fix, once and for all, a nonzero element \(W_S \in C_c^\infty(F_S^\times)\). For \(\tau \in F^\times\), define the linear map \(\heartsuit^{\tau} : C_c^\infty(\operatorname{PB}^\times_S) \rightarrow \mathcal{S}(B_S)\) by \[\heartsuit^{\tau} f(x) := \frac{W_S(\tau \mathop{\mathrm{nr}}(x))}{|\tau \mathop{\mathrm{nr}}(x)|_S} 1_{B_S^\times}(x) f(\mathop{\mathrm{pr}}(x)),\] where \(\mathop{\mathrm{pr}}: B_S^\times \rightarrow \operatorname{PB}^\times_S\) denotes the natural projection.

§5.3. Statement of main result

The statement involves the metaplectic group (§4.4.1) and the Weil representation (§4.4.3). For \(s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(F_S)\), we abbreviate \(\rho^{\tau}(s) := \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}^{\psi^{\tau},B}(s)\) and \(\rho_0^\tau(s) := \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}^{\psi^{\tau},B^0}(s)\); these operators act respectively on \(\mathcal{S}(B_S)\) and \(\mathcal{S}(B_S^0)\). The operators \(1 \otimes \rho_0^{\tau_i}(s)\) on \(\mathcal{S}(B_S)\) are defined using the decomposition \(B_S = F_S \oplus B_S^0\), as in §3.2.4.

Theorem 4. There is a finite subset \(X\) of \(F^\times\) and a finite collection \((\varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2})_{\tau_1,\tau_2 \in X}\) of sesquilinear forms \(\varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2} : \mathcal{S}(B_S) \otimes \mathcal{S}(B_S) \otimes \mathcal{A}_0^S \otimes \mathcal{A}_0^S \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\), depending only upon \(F\), \(\psi\), \(S\) and \(W_S\), with the following properties:

  1. Relevance. For \(f \in C_c^\infty(\operatorname{PB}^\times_S)\), one has the following identity of sesquilinear forms on \(\mathcal{A}_0^S\): \[\label{eq:relevance}\tag{5.2} \mathcal{V}_f = \mathcal{M}_f + \sum_{\tau_1,\tau_2 \in X} \varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\heartsuit^{\tau_1} f, \heartsuit^{\tau_2} f, \cdot, \cdot).\]

  2. \(\operatorname{O}_1(F)\)-invariance. \[\varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\mathfrak{S} \phi_1, \phi_2, \Psi_1, \Psi_2) = \varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2}( \phi_1, \phi_2, \Psi_1, \Psi_2),\] \[\varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\phi_1, \mathfrak{S}\phi_2, \Psi_1, \Psi_2) = \varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\phi_1, \phi_2, \Psi_1, \Psi_2).\]

  3. \(\mathop{\mathrm{SO}}(B_S^0)\)-invariance. For \(g_1,g_2 \in \operatorname{PB}^\times_S\), \[\varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g_1) \phi_1, \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g_2) \phi_2, \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{reg}}}(g_1) \Psi_1, \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{reg}}}(g_2) \Psi_2)\] \[= \varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\phi_1, \phi_2, \Psi_1, \Psi_2).\]

  4. Metaplectic invariance. For \(s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(F_S)\), \[\varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\rho^{\tau_1}(s) \phi_1, \rho^{\tau_2}(s) \phi_2, \Psi_1, \Psi_2) = \varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\phi_1, \phi_2, \Psi_1, \Psi_2).\]

  5. Main estimate. For \(s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(F_S)\), \[\varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2}((1 \otimes \rho_0^{\tau_1}(s)) \phi_1, (1 \otimes \rho_0^{\tau_2}(s)) \phi_2, \Psi_1, \Psi_2)\] \[\ll \Xi(s) \prod_{i=1,2} \mathcal{C}(\phi_i) \|\Psi_i\|_{L^1},\] where \(\Xi\) denotes the Harish–Chandra function (§4.1.4) and \(\mathcal{C}(\phi_i)\) denotes a quantity that varies continuously with \(\phi_i\) (see §4.5.1). The implied constants and the uniformity in the continuity of \(\mathcal{C}(.)\) depend at most upon \(F,\psi,S,W_S\).

  6. Construction. \(\varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2}\) factors explicitly through the theta correspondence in the sense of §5.4.9.

The proof of Theorem 4 occupies §5.4.

Remark 6. In applications of Theorem 4, the crucial assertions are the relevance and the main estimate. The \(\mathop{\mathrm{SO}}(B_S^0)\)-invariance may be employed to obtain quantitatively stronger estimates, the \(\operatorname{O}_1(F)\)-invariance and metaplectic invariance may be computationally convenient (see (Nelson 2017)), and the construction may be useful for further refinements and extensions.

Remark 7. The formulation of Theorem 4 is independent of the choice of measures on \(\operatorname{PB}_S^\times\) and on \([\operatorname{PB}^\times]\).

Remark 8. Theorem 4 minus the “main estimate” is like a trace formula: \(\mathcal{V}_f\) is a sum over automorphic forms, \(\mathcal{M}_f\) is the “identity” or “diagonal” contribution, and the \(\varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2}\) are the “interesting” contributions which one often wishes to show are small. One difference is that \(\mathcal{V}_f\) has a quadrilinear (rather than bilinear) dependence upon the automorphic forms \(\varphi\).

Remark 9. Theorem 4 likely extends to the split case \(B = M_2(F)\) after incorporating contributions from the continuous spectrum into the definitions of §5.2 and replacing \(\|\Psi_i\|_{L^1}\) with \(\|{\mathop{\mathrm{ht}}}^A \Psi_i\|_{L^1}\) for some fixed large enough \(A > 0\).

§5.4. Proof of Theorem 4

§5.4.1. Measures

With a view to applications, we have formulated Theorem 4 in a measure-independent fashion. For the proof, it is convenient to take on \([\operatorname{PB}^\times]\) the Tamagawa measure, so that \[\label{eq:defn-of-c-2}\tag{5.3} c_3 = \frac{1}{2} \zeta_F^{(S)}(2),\] and to fix measures on \(\operatorname{PB}^\times_{\mathbb{A}}, \operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathfrak{p}\) and hence on \(\operatorname{PB}^\times_S = \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \in S} \operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathfrak{p}\) as in §4.1.3.

§5.4.2. The \(\heartsuit\) operator: local

Suppose temporarily (for §5.4.2 only) that \(k\) is a local field, \(\psi\) is a nontrivial unitary character of \(k\), \(B\) is a quaternion algebra over \(k\), \(G := B^\times / k^\times\), and \(W \in C_c^\infty(k^\times)\). Recall from §3.2.5 the definition of \(\Omega\). We define a linear map \(\heartsuit : C_c^\infty(G) \rightarrow \Omega\) by \[\heartsuit f(t,x) := \frac{W(t \mathop{\mathrm{nr}}(x))}{|t \mathop{\mathrm{nr}}(x)|} 1_{B^\times}(x) f(x).\] (By abuse of notation, we write \(f(x)\) for the value taken by \(f\) at the image of \(x\) under the natural projection \(B^\times \rightarrow G\).)

By inspecting the definitions, one has the identities of maps \(C_c^\infty(G) \rightarrow \Omega\) \[\mathfrak{S} \heartsuit = \heartsuit \mathfrak{S}, \quad \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) \heartsuit = \heartsuit \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) \text{ (for $g \in G$)}.\] By inspecting the definitions, one has for \(y \in k^\times, b \in B^\times\) that \[\label{eqn:local-heartsuit-formula}\tag{5.5} \rho_{\mathop{\mathrm{Weil}}}(a(y)) \heartsuit f(\mathop{\mathrm{nr}}(b)^{-1},b) = |y| \heartsuit f(y \mathop{\mathrm{nr}}(b)^{-1}, b) = W(y) f(b).\] By the formula \((3.7)\) for \(\|.\|_{\Omega}\), one obtains \[\label{eqn:local-norm-heartsuit-f}\tag{5.6} \|\heartsuit f\|_{\Omega} = \|f\|_{L^2(G)} \, \|W\|_{L^2(k^\times, |x|^{-1} \, d x)}.\]

§5.4.3. The \(\heartsuit\) operator: global

We revert to the global setting of §5. Let \(\pi \in A_0^S\). Recall from §4.6.1 the definition of \(\Omega\). We define a linear map \(\heartsuit : C_c^\infty(\operatorname{PB}^\times_S) \rightarrow \Omega\) by \[\heartsuit f(t,x) := \frac{W_S(t_S \mathop{\mathrm{nr}}(x_S))}{|t_S \mathop{\mathrm{nr}}(x_S)|} 1_{B_S^\times}(x_S) f(x_S) \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} \mathop{\mathrm{vol}}(K_{\mathfrak{p}})^{-1} \phi_\mathfrak{p}^0(t_\mathfrak{p},x_\mathfrak{p}),\] where \(\phi_\mathfrak{p}^0 \in \Omega_\mathfrak{p}\) is defined with respect to \(R_\mathfrak{p}\) (see §3.2.6). This definition and that of §5.2.4 are obviously similar; we record their precise relationship below in §5.4.9.

By \((5.5)\) and the lemma of §3.4.1, one has for \(y \in \mathbb{A}^\times\), \(b \in B_\mathbb{A}^\times\) that \[\label{eqn:formulas-for-heartsuit-f-global}\tag{5.7} |y| \heartsuit f( y \mathop{\mathrm{nr}}(b)^{-1}, b) = W_S(y_S) f(b_S) \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} T_{y_\mathfrak{p}}(b_\mathfrak{p}),\] with \(T_{y_\mathfrak{p}}\) as in §3.4.1. By combining \((5.6)\) with Lemma 1 of §3.2.6, one obtains \[\label{eqn:norm-of-heartsuit-f-global}\tag{5.8} \|\heartsuit f\|^2_{\Omega} = \|f\|_{L^2(\operatorname{PB}^\times_S)}^2 \int_{t \in F_S^\times} |W_S|^2(t) \, \frac{d t}{|t|} \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} \frac{\mathop{\mathrm{vol}}(R_\mathfrak{p})}{\mathop{\mathrm{vol}}(K_\mathfrak{p})^2}.\]

Lemma 14. Let \(\pi \in A_0^S\). Let \(\Psi_1,\Psi_2 \in \pi\) be \(\prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} K_\mathfrak{p}\)-invariant vectors. For \(f \in C_c^\infty(\operatorname{PB}^\times_S)\), the quantity \(\mathfrak{m}(\heartsuit f, \heartsuit f, \Psi_1, \Psi_2)\) (see §4.7.3) equals \[c_2 L^{(S)}(\pi,\tfrac{1}{2}) \int_{g \in \operatorname{PB}_S^\times} \langle \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) \mathfrak{S} f, \mathfrak{S} f \rangle_{L^2(\operatorname{PB}_S^\times)} \langle \pi(g) \Psi_1, \Psi_2 \rangle_{\operatorname{PB}^\times} \,d g,\] where \[\label{eq:defn-c2-frak-W}\tag{5.9} c_2 := \frac{1}{\zeta^{(S)}_F(2)} \left(\prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} \frac{\mathop{\mathrm{vol}}(R_\mathfrak{p})}{\mathop{\mathrm{vol}}(K_\mathfrak{p})}\right) \int_{y \in F_S^\times} |W_S|^2(y) \, \frac{d y}{|y|}.\]

Proof. By the lemma of §4.7.3, the polarization of \((5.8)\) and the commutativity \(\heartsuit \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) = \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) \heartsuit\), the required identity holds if we replace \(S\) with some possibly larger finite set of places \(S' \supseteq S\). To deduce the identity as written, we apply \((3.14)\) (using \((4.5)\) to verify its hypotheses). ◻

§5.4.4. A specific Eichler/Jacquet–Langlands lift

For \(\pi \in A_0^S\), let \(\Phi_\pi \in \pi_{\mathop{\mathrm{JL}}}\) denote the element of the Jacquet–Langlands lift of \(\pi\) having the Fourier expansion \(\Phi_\pi(n(x) a(y)) = \sum_{\tau \in F^\times} \psi(\tau x) W_\pi(\tau y)\), where the Whittaker function \(W_\pi : \mathbb{A}^\times \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) is given by \(W_\pi(y) := W_S(y_S) \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} W_{\pi_\mathfrak{p}}^0(y_\mathfrak{p})\) (see §4.2.1, §4.2.2).

Lemma 15. One has \(\|\Phi_\pi\|^2 = c_1 L^{(S)}(\mathop{\mathrm{ad}}\pi,1)\), where \[\label{eq:c-of-frak-W-defn}\tag{5.10} c_1 := \frac{2}{ \zeta_F^{(S)}(2)} \left(\prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} \Delta_{\psi_{\mathfrak{p}}}^{-1/2}\right) \int_{y \in F_S^\times} |W_S|^2(y) \, \frac{d y}{|y|}.\] If \(\pi, \pi ' \in A_0^S\) are distinct, then \(\langle \Phi_{\pi}, \Phi_{\pi '} \rangle = 0\).

Proof. The conclusion in the case \(\pi \neq \pi '\) is the multiplicity one theorem for \(\operatorname{PB}^\times\) combined with the injectivity of \(\pi \mapsto \pi_{\mathop{\mathrm{JL}}}\). The formula \((5.10)\) is a consequence of the lemma of §4.2.2 and the corresponding local calculation (§3.3). ◻

§5.4.5. The normalizing scalar

Recall from \((5.10)\), \((5.9)\) and \((5.3)\) the scalars \(c_1,c_2,c_3\). By the local volume formulas of §3.1.3, \[\label{eqn:relation-c1-c2-c}\tag{5.11} c_1^{-1} c_2 = c_3.\]

§5.4.6. Application of the pretrace formula

Recall the theta functions \(\Theta(\phi,\Psi)\) attached in §4.6 to each \(\phi \in \Omega, \Psi \in \mathcal{A}_0\). Let \(f \in C_c^\infty(\operatorname{PB}^\times_S)\), \(\Psi \in \mathcal{A}_0^S\).

Lemma 10. \(\sum_{\pi \in A_0^S} |\omega_\pi( f,\Psi)| \| \Phi_\pi \|_{L^p([\operatorname{PGL}_2])} < \infty\) for \(p=2,\infty\).

Proof. By \((4.7)\) and \((4.8)\), it suffices to show that \(\| \Phi_\pi \|_{L^p([\operatorname{PGL}_2])} \ll C(\pi)^{O(1)}\). The case \(p=2\) follows from the lemma of §5.4.4 and \((4.10)\). The case \(p=\infty\) reduces to the case \(p=2\) by axioms (S2a) and (S3b) of (Michel and Venkatesh 2010, sec. 2.4), wherein the quantities \(\mathcal{S}_d(\Phi_\pi)\) may be estimated using (Michel and Venkatesh 2010, sec. 3.2.5). A direct proof of this convergence also follows by a rearrangement of the arguments given below. ◻

Lemma 11. \(\Theta(\heartsuit f,\Psi) = \sum_{\pi \in A_0^S} \omega_\pi( f,\Psi) \Phi_\pi\).

Proof. Set \(\Phi_1 := \Theta(\heartsuit f,\Psi)\) and \(\Phi_2 := \sum_{\pi \in A_0^S} \omega_\pi( f,\Psi) \Phi_\pi\); we must show that \(\Phi_1 = \Phi_2\). Since \(\Phi_1, \Phi_2\) are cuspidal, it will suffice to demonstrate the equality of their Whittaker functions \(W_1, W_2 : \mathbb{A}^\times \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) as defined in §4.2.1. By the lemma of §4.6.3 and \((5.7)\), we have \[W_1(y) = \sum_{\gamma \in \operatorname{PB}^\times} \int_{g \in [\operatorname{PB}^\times]} \Psi(g) W_S(y_S) f(g_S^{-1} \gamma g_S) \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} T_{y_\mathfrak{p}}(g_\mathfrak{p}^{-1} \gamma g_\mathfrak{p}) \,d g.\] The definition of \(\Phi_\pi\) implies (using Lemma 1 to justify the interchange of summation with the Fourier integral over the compact group \(\mathbb{A}/F\)) that \[W_2(y) = \sum_{\pi \in A_0^S} \omega_\pi( f,\Psi) W_S(y_S) \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} W_{\pi_\mathfrak{p}}^0(y_\mathfrak{p}).\] Since \(\Psi \in \mathcal{A}_0^S\), we have \(\omega_\pi(f,\Psi) = 0\) for all \(\pi \in A^S\) with \(\pi \notin A_0^S\), so it suffices to establish for all \(y \in \mathbb{A}^\times\), \(g \in \operatorname{PB}^\times_{\mathbb{A}}\) the pointwise identity \[\sum_{\gamma \in \operatorname{PB}^\times} f(g_S^{-1} \gamma g_S) \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} T_{y_\mathfrak{p}}(g_\mathfrak{p}^{-1} \gamma g_\mathfrak{p}) = \sum_{\pi \in A^S} \sum_{\varphi \in \mathcal{B}(\pi \cap \mathcal{A}^S)} \overline{\varphi}(g) \pi(f) \varphi(g) \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} W_{\pi_\mathfrak{p}}^0(y_\mathfrak{p}),\] which follows from the pretrace formula (§4.3.2) and the identity \(W_{\pi_\mathfrak{p}}^0(y_\mathfrak{p}) = \lambda_{\pi_\mathfrak{p}}(T_{y_\mathfrak{p}})\) (see \((3.13)\)). ◻

Remark 5. Lemma 2 and its proof are in the spirit of arguments of Shimizu (Shimizu 1972, sec. 4), but we were unable to relate them precisely (e.g., by deducing one from the other).

§5.4.7. Some sesquilinear forms

Define \(\mathcal{V}, \mathcal{M}, \mathcal{E} : \Omega \otimes \Omega \otimes \mathcal{A}_0 \otimes \mathcal{A}_0 \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) by requiring that for \(\phi_1, \phi_2 \in \Omega\) satisfying \(\phi_i[y] = \phi_i'[y] \otimes \phi_i''[y]\) with \(\phi_i'[y] \in \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{A})\) and \(\phi_i''[y] \in \mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A}^0)\) for all \(y \in \mathbb{A}^\times\), one has with the abbreviations \(\theta_i := \theta_{\psi^{\tau_i}}(\phi_i'[\tau_i y])\) and \(h_i := \theta_{\psi^{\tau_i}}(\phi_i''[\tau_i y],\Psi_i)\) that \[\mathcal{V}(\phi_1,\phi_2,\Psi_1,\Psi_2) := c_1^{-1} \int_{y \in \mathbb{A}^\times / F^\times \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}} |y|^2 \frac { 1 } { 2^2 } \sum_{\tau_1,\tau_2 \in F^\times / F^{\times 2}} \langle \theta_1 h_1, \theta_2 h_2 \rangle \, d_2^\times y,\] \[\mathcal{M}(\phi_1,\phi_2,\Psi_1,\Psi_2) := c_1^{-1} \int_{y \in \mathbb{A}^\times / F^\times \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}} |y|^2 \frac { 1 } { 2^2 } \sum_{\tau_1,\tau_2 \in F^\times / F^{\times 2}} \langle \theta_1, \theta_2 \rangle \langle h_1, h_2 \rangle \, d_2^\times y\] and \(\mathcal{E} := \mathcal{V} - \mathcal{M}\), or equivalently, \[\mathcal{E}(\phi_1,\phi_2,\cdot ,\cdot ) := c_1^{-1} \int_{y \in \mathbb{A}^\times / F^\times \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}} |y|^2 \frac { 1 } { 2^2 } \sum_{\tau_1,\tau_2 \in F^\times / F^{\times 2}} \mathcal{E}_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\phi_1[\tau_1 y], \phi_2[\tau_2 y],\cdot,\cdot ) \, d_2^\times y,\] where \(\mathcal{E}_{\tau_1,\tau_2} : \mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A}) \otimes \mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A}) \otimes \mathcal{A}_0 \otimes \mathcal{A}_0 \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) is as in §4.5.6. The definitions makes sense for the same reasons as in §4.7.3. The identity \[\label{eqn:c1-times-error-equals-bla}\tag{5.13} \mathcal{V}(\phi_1,\phi_2,\Psi_1,\Psi_2) = c_1^{-1} \langle \Theta(\phi_1, \Psi_1), \Theta(\phi_2, \Psi_2) \rangle.\] follows from §4.6.5 when \(\phi\) is a pure tensor, hence in general by linearity.

§5.4.8. The main identities

Proposition 2. Let \(f \in C_c^\infty(\operatorname{PB}^\times_S)\) and \(\Psi_1,\Psi_2 \in \mathcal{A}_0^S\). Then \[\label{eq:V-equals-Vf}\tag{5.14} \mathcal{V}(\heartsuit f,\heartsuit f,\Psi_1,\Psi_2) = \mathcal{V}_f(\Psi_1,\Psi_2),\] \[\label{eq:M-equals-Mf}\tag{5.15} \mathcal{M}(\heartsuit f,\heartsuit f,\Psi_1,\Psi_2) = \mathcal{M}_f(\Psi_1,\Psi_2),\] \[\label{eq:Vf-equals-Mf-plus-E}\tag{5.16} \mathcal{V}_f(\Psi_1,\Psi_2) = \mathcal{M}_f(\Psi_1,\Psi_2) + \mathcal{E}(\heartsuit f, \heartsuit f, \Psi_1, \Psi_2).\]

Proof. \((5.14)\): By \((5.13)\), Lemma 2 of §5.4.6, and the lemma of §5.4.4, \[\begin{align} \mathcal{V}(\heartsuit f,\heartsuit f,\Psi_1,\Psi_2) &= c_1^{-1} \langle \Theta(\heartsuit f, \Psi_1), \Theta(\heartsuit f, \Psi_2) \rangle \\ &= c_1^{-1} \sum_{\pi_1,\pi_2 \in A_0^S} \left\langle \omega_{\pi_1}(f, \Psi_1), \omega_{\pi_2}(f, \Psi_2) \right\rangle \\ &= \sum_{\pi \in A_0^S} L^{(S)}(\mathop{\mathrm{ad}}\pi,1) \omega_{\pi}( f, \Psi_1), \overline{\omega_{\pi}( f, \Psi_2)} \\ &= V_f(\Psi_1,\Psi_2). \end{align}\]

\((5.15)\): by the lemma of §5.4.3 and \((5.11)\).

\((5.16)\): by \((5.14)\), \((5.15)\) and the definition of \(\mathcal{E}\). ◻

§5.4.9. Completion of the proof

We now apply Proposition 1 (see §4.5.6) and Proposition 2 to prove Theorem 4. The purpose of this final, purely technical part of the argument is to recast the content of those propositions in terms of \(\mathcal{S}(B_S)\) rather than the less “user-friendly” space \(\Omega\).

By weak approximation, we may choose a compact fundamental domain \(Y \subset \mathbb{A}^\times / \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}\) for \(\mathbb{A}^\times / F^{\times} \mathbb{A}^{\times 2}\) with the property that \(y_\mathfrak{p} = 1\) for all \(y \in Y\) and \(\mathfrak{p} \in S\). Choose a finite set \(X \subseteq F^\times\) of representatives for the finite set \[\label{eq:elements-such-that-multiplying-by-something-in-Y-gives-squares-mod-units-outside-S}\tag{5.17} \{\tau \in F^\times / F^{\times 2} : \text{ there exists } y \in Y \text{ so that } y_\mathfrak{p} \tau \in F_\mathfrak{p}^{\times 2} \mathcal{O}_\mathfrak{p}^\times \text{ for all } \mathfrak{p} \notin S \}.\] For \(y \in Y, \tau \in X\), let \(\diamondsuit^{\tau y} : \mathcal{S}(B_S) \hookrightarrow \mathcal{S}(B_\mathbb{A})\) denote the map \(\diamondsuit^{y \tau} \Phi := \Phi \otimes (\otimes_{\mathfrak{p} \notin S} \phi_\mathfrak{p}^0[\tau y_\mathfrak{p} ])\), where \(\phi_{\mathfrak{p}}^0 \in \Omega_{\mathfrak{p}}\) denotes as usual the distinguished element. For \(f \in C_c^\infty(\operatorname{PB}_S^\times)\), one then has \(\diamondsuit^{\tau y} \heartsuit^{\tau} f = \heartsuit f[\tau y]\). Observe that for \(\mathfrak{p} \notin S\) and \(t \in F_\mathfrak{p}^\times\), one has \(\phi_\mathfrak{p}^0[t] = 0\) unless \(t \in F_\mathfrak{p}^{\times 2} \mathcal{O}_\mathfrak{p}^\times\). It follows that for \(\tau \in F^\times\) and \(y \in Y\), one has \(\heartsuit f[\tau y] = 0\) unless \(\tau\) belongs to the set \((5.17)\), hence that \[\label{eq:penultimate-identity-before-proving-main-general-thm}\tag{5.18} \mathcal{E}(\heartsuit f, \heartsuit f, \cdot, \cdot) = \frac{c_1^{-1}}{2^2} \int_{y \in Y} |y|^2 \sum_{\tau_1,\tau_2 \in X} \mathcal{E}_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\diamondsuit^{\tau_1 y} \heartsuit^{\tau_1} f, \diamondsuit^{\tau_2 y} \heartsuit^{\tau_2} f, \cdot,\cdot) \, d_2^\times y.\] Define \(\varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2} : \mathcal{S}(B_S) \otimes \mathcal{S}(B_S) \otimes \mathcal{A}_0^S \otimes \mathcal{A}_0^S \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) by \[\label{eq:defn-of-the-eps-guys-yay}\tag{5.19} \varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\Phi_1,\Phi_2,\Psi_1,\Psi_2) := \frac{c_1^{-1}}{2^2} \int_{y \in Y} |y|^2 \mathcal{E}_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\diamondsuit^{\tau_1 y} \Phi_1, \diamondsuit^{\tau_2 y} \Phi_2, \Psi_1,\Psi_2) \, d_2^\times y.\] We verify the assertions made in Theorem 4:

  1. The “relevance” follows from \((5.18)\), \((5.19)\) and Proposition 2.

  2. Since \(\mathfrak{S} \phi_\mathfrak{p}^0 = \phi_\mathfrak{p}^0\), one has \(\mathfrak{S} \diamondsuit^{\tau_i y} = \diamondsuit^{\tau_i y} \mathfrak{S}\). For \(g \in \operatorname{PB}^\times_S\) and \(s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(F_S)\), one has \(\mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) \diamondsuit^{\tau_i y} = \diamondsuit^{\tau_i y} \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g)\) and \(\rho^{\tau_i}(s) \diamondsuit^{\tau_i y} = \diamondsuit^{\tau_i y} \rho^{\tau_i}(s)\). Thus the “\(\operatorname{O}_1(F)\)-invariance,” “\(\mathop{\mathrm{SO}}(B_S^0)\)-invariance” and “metaplectic invariance” follow from §4.5.7.

  3. The “main estimate” is the content of Proposition 1.

§5.5. Classicalization

We now specialize to the setting of Theorem 1 and record how Theorem 4 specializes to Theorem 3.

§5.5.1. Specialization to a single place

We specialize the definitions of §5.2 to the case that ramification is concentrated at a single place \(\mathfrak{q}\) of \(F\), finite or infinite. This is the case required for the proof of Theorem 1 as well as its non-archimedean analogue pursued in (Nelson 2017).

Assume that \(S\) is the set of places \(\mathfrak{p}\) for which either

  • \(\mathfrak{p}\) is infinite,

  • \(\mathfrak{p}\) is a finite place at which \(B\) ramifies, or

  • \(\mathfrak{p} = \mathfrak{q}\).

Assume that for each \(\mathfrak{p} \in S - \{\mathfrak{q}\}\), the completion \(B_\mathfrak{p}\) is non-split, or equivalently, that \(\operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathfrak{p}\) is compact. There are the following possibilities:

  1. \(\mathfrak{q}\) is real, in which case \(F\) is totally real and \(B\) ramifies at every infinite place other than \(\mathfrak{q}\).

  2. \(\mathfrak{q}\) is complex, in which case \(F\) is real and \(B\) ramifies at every infinite place other than \(\mathfrak{q}\).

  3. \(\mathfrak{q}\) is finite, in which case \(F\) is totally real and \(B\) is totally definite.

For each place \(\mathfrak{p}\), define the compact open subgroup \(J_\mathfrak{p} \leqslant\operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathfrak{p}\) as in §3.4 by taking for \(J_\mathfrak{p}\) the image of \(R_\mathfrak{p}^\times\) if \(\mathfrak{p}\) is finite and taking \(J_\mathfrak{p} := \operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathfrak{p}\) if \(\mathfrak{p}\) is infinite. Set \(J := \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \neq \mathfrak{q}} J_\mathfrak{p}\). In addition to the notation of §5.1, we now introduce a superscripted \(J\), as in \(\mathcal{A}^J, \mathcal{A}_0^J, \pi^J\) to denote the \(J\)-fixed subspace. We denote by \(\mathcal{A}^J_+ \subseteq \mathcal{A}^J\), \(\mathcal{A}^J_{0+} \subseteq \mathcal{A}_0^J\) the “even” subspaces consisting of \(\varphi\) that are \(\operatorname{PB}^\times_{\mathfrak{p}}\)-invariant for all \(\mathfrak{p} \in S - \{\mathfrak{q}\}\). Thus, for instance, \(\mathcal{A}_{0+}^J \subseteq \mathcal{A}_0^J \subseteq \mathcal{A}_0^S \subseteq \mathcal{A}_0 \subseteq \mathcal{A}\). We denote by \(A_0, A^J, A_0^J, A^J_+, A^J_{0+}\) the set of all \(\pi \in A\) having nonzero intersection with the space having the corresponding scripted notation.

Set \(G := \operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathfrak{q}\), and let \(f \in C_c^\infty(G)\). For \(\mathfrak{p} \in S - \{q\}\), set \(e_{J_\mathfrak{p}} := \mathop{\mathrm{vol}}(J_\mathfrak{p})^{-1} 1_{J_\mathfrak{p}} \in C_c^\infty(\operatorname{PB}^\times_\mathfrak{p})\). Define \(\tilde{f} \in C_c^\infty(\operatorname{PB}^\times_S)\) by the formula \[\tilde{f} (g) := f(g_\mathfrak{q}) \prod_{\mathfrak{p} \in S - \{\mathfrak{q} \}} e_{J_\mathfrak{p}}(g_\mathfrak{p}).\] For \(\pi \in A_0^J\) and \(\Psi \in \mathcal{A}_0^J\), set \(\omega_\pi(f,\Psi) := \sum_{\varphi \in \mathcal{B}(\pi \cap \mathcal{A}^J)} \langle \varphi, \Psi \cdot \pi(f) \varphi \rangle\). Then \(\omega_\pi(\tilde{f},\Psi) = \omega_\pi(f,\Psi)\) (see §5.2.1 for the definition of the left hand side). Since \(\dim(\pi_\mathfrak{p}) = 1\) for all \(\mathfrak{p} \in S - \{\mathfrak{q} \}\), one has for \(\Psi \in \pi' \in \mathcal{A}_0^J\) that \(\omega_\pi(f,\Psi) = 0\) unless \(\pi ' \in \mathcal{A}_{0+}^J\).

Let \(V_{f}, M_{f} : \mathcal{A}_{0+}^J \otimes \mathcal{A}_{0+}^J \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\) denote the sesquilinear forms obtained by restricting the forms \(\mathcal{V}_{\tilde{f}}, \mathcal{M}_{\tilde{f}} : \mathcal{A}_0^S \otimes \mathcal{A}_0^S \rightarrow \mathbb{C}\). Then \[V_{f}(\Psi_1,\Psi_2) = \sum_{\pi \in A_0^J} L^{(S)}(\mathop{\mathrm{ad}}\pi,1) \omega_\pi(f,\Psi_1) \overline{\omega_\pi(f,\Psi_2)}.\] By the observation that \(\mathfrak{S} e_{J_\mathfrak{p} } = e_{J_\mathfrak{p}}\) for \(\mathfrak{p} \in S - \{\mathfrak{q}\}\) and the local calculations \((3.15)\) and \((3.16)\), we see that for \(\Psi_1 \in \pi_1 \in A_{0+}^J\) and \(\Psi_2 \in \pi_2 \in A_{0+}^J\), we have \(M_{f}(\Psi_1,\Psi_2) = 0\) unless \(\pi_1 = \pi_2 =: \pi\), in which case \[M_{f}(\Psi_1,\Psi_2) = c_4 L^{(S)}(\pi,\tfrac{1}{2}) \int_{g \in G} \langle \mathop{\mathrm{Ad}}(g) \mathfrak{S} f, \mathfrak{S} f \rangle_{L^2(G)} \langle \pi(g) \Psi_1, \Psi_2 \rangle_{\operatorname{PB}^\times} \,d g\] where \[\label{eq:defn-of-c4}\tag{5.22} c_4 := 2^t \zeta_F^{(S)}(2) \mathop{\mathrm{vol}}([\operatorname{PB}^\times])^{-1}.\] with \(t\) the number of finite primes \(\mathfrak{p} \in S - \{\mathfrak{q}\}\).

§5.5.2. Strong approximation

Retaining the notation of §5.5.1, we record here how the quotient \([\operatorname{PB}^\times]/J\) unadelizes under some assumptions. Recall that \(G := \operatorname{PB}^\times_{\mathfrak{q}}\). Let \(\Gamma \leqslant G\) denote the image of \(\operatorname{PB}^\times \cap J\) under the inclusion \(\operatorname{PB}^\times \hookrightarrow G\). Then \(\Gamma\) is a discrete cocompact subgroup of \(G\), and the natural map \(\iota : \Gamma \backslash G \rightarrow [\operatorname{PB}^\times]/J\) is injective. We record a standard consequence of strong approximation.

Lemma 16. Suppose that \(F\) has odd narrow class number and either that

  1. \(B_\mathfrak{q}\) is split, or that

  2. \(\mathfrak{q}\) is infinite and \(B\) has class number one.

Then \(\iota\) is bijective.

§5.5.3. Proof of Theorem 3

We assume now that \(\mathfrak{q}\) is archimedean, so that the above setting recovers that of §1.5. We deduce Theorem 3 by specializing (parts of) Theorem 4, following the unadelization procedure discussed above. For \(f \in C_c^\infty(\operatorname{PB}_\mathfrak{q}^\times)\), we have \[\mathcal{V}(f) = V_f(\Psi_1,\Psi_2) = V_{\tilde{f}}(\Psi_1,\Psi_2),\] and similarly for \(\mathcal{M}(f)\). Here \(\mathcal{V}(f)\) is as defined in §1.8, while \(\mathcal{V}_f\) and \(\mathcal{V}_{\tilde{f}}\) are as in §5.5.1. We identify \(\tau \in F ^\times\) with its image in \(\mathbb{R}^\times\) via the given archimedean place \(\mathfrak{q}\). Inspecting the definitions, we have \(\heartsuit^{\tau} \tilde{f} = (\heartsuit^{\tau} f) \otimes \Phi^{\tau}\), where \(\heartsuit^{\tau} f \in \mathcal{S}(B_\mathfrak{q})\) is defined by \(\heartsuit^{\tau} f (g) := W(\tau \mathop{\mathrm{nr}}(g)) f(g)\) and \(\Phi^{\tau} = \otimes_{\mathfrak{p} \in S - \{\mathfrak{q} \}} \Phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\tau}\) for some \(\Phi_\mathfrak{p}^{\tau} \in \mathcal{S} (B_\mathfrak{p} )\) not depending upon \(f\). The required identity \((1.13)\) then holds with \(\mathcal{E}_{\tau_1,\tau_2}(\phi) := \varepsilon_{\tau_1,\tau_2} (\phi \otimes \Phi^{\tau_1}, \phi \otimes \Phi^{\tau_2}, \Psi_1, \Psi_2)\).

To deduce the claimed error estimate \((1.14)\), we specialize the main estimate \((1.14)\) of Theorem 4 to the case that \(s \in {\mathop{\mathrm{Mp}}}_2(F_S)\) lifts the diagonal element \(\mathop{\mathrm{diag}}(y,y^{-1})\) of \({\mathop{\mathrm{SL}}}_2(F_\mathfrak{q})\). Then \(\rho_0^\tau(s)\) (§3.2.3) acts on \(\mathcal{S}(B_S)\) via the factor \(\mathcal{S}(B_\mathfrak{q})\), where it acts by a constant multiple of the dilation operator \(D_y\) defined in §1.8. The relevant estimates for \(\Xi(s)\) were recorded in §3.1.5.

§2. Application to microlocal lifts

Our aim is now to prove Theorem 1 by application of Theorem 3. We retain the general notation of §1.5 (in particular, \(G = \operatorname{PGL}_2(\mathbb{R})\), \(\Gamma < G\) is an arithmetic subgroup, and \(A_0\) is the set of nontrivial irreducible representations \(\pi \subseteq L^2(\Gamma \backslash G)\) of both the group \(G\) and the Hecke operators \(T_p\)) and the asymptotic notation and conventions of §1.10 (in particular, the conventions concerning “\(\mathop{\mathrm{h}}\)-dependent elements” and “fixed”).

The microlocal lift measures \(\mu_\pi\) are defined (§6.5) using differential operators (namely, raising and lowering operators), but our methods apply most naturally to the distributions \(\mu(\pi(f), \cdot)\) attached in §1.8 to integral operators \(\pi(f)\), \(f \in C_c^\infty(G)\). Our first main task is thus to give an alternative construction of the microlocal lift measures using integral operators. One input here is the microlocal calculus for Lie group representations developed in (Nelson and Venkatesh 2021), whose specialization to \(\operatorname{PGL}_2(\mathbb{R})\) we recall in §6.7. Having constructed microlocal lift measures in this way, we are in good position to apply Theorem 3, and must then estimate the “main” and “error” terms that arise. We refer back to §1.10 for a more detailed survey of Part .

§6. Archimedean preliminaries

§6.1. Lie algebra

Let \(\mathfrak{g}\) denote the Lie algebra of \(G\). We denote by \(\mathfrak{g}_\mathbb{C} \cong \mathfrak{s}\mathfrak{l}_2(\mathbb{C})\) its complexification and by \(\mathfrak{g}_\mathbb{C}^*\) the complex dual. We will often identity \(\mathfrak{g}_\mathbb{C}\) with the space of linear functions on \(\mathfrak{g}_\mathbb{C}^*\). We work with the following basis elements for \(\mathfrak{g}_{\mathbb{C}}\): \[X := \frac{1}{2 i} \begin{pmatrix} 1 & i \\ i & -1 \end{pmatrix}, \quad Y := \frac{1}{2 i} \begin{pmatrix} 1 & -i \\ -i & -1 \end{pmatrix}, \quad W := \frac{1}{2 i} \begin{pmatrix} 0 & 1 \\ -1 & 0 \end{pmatrix}.\] These satisfy \([X,Y] = - 2W\), \([W,X]= X\) and \([W,Y]= -Y\). The map \(\theta \mapsto e^{i \theta W}\) defines an isomorphism from \(\mathbb{R}/2 \pi \mathbb{Z}\) to \(K^1\). The complex conjugation on \(\mathfrak{g}_\mathbb{C}\) is given by \(-\overline{X} = Y\) and \(- \overline{W} = W\).
